## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard object of chemical kinetics. With only t and A available, the most likely models are autonomous or weakly non-autonomous rate laws (e.g., order-based kinetics, reversible relaxation to equilibrium, or time-varying effective rate constants).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; surface/photolysis-limited regimes)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular or pseudo-first-order consumption)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or dimerization-like kinetics with only A observed)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order / complex mechanism lumping)
- Approach to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (reversible reaction with equilibrium concentration c1)
- Mixed-order (linear + quadratic): dA_dt = -(c0 * A + c1 * A**2) (parallel first- and second-order pathways)
- Self-inhibition / crowding rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective rate decreases at high A due to inhibition/transport limits)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-in-A form: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth followed by depletion/limitation in A)
- Time-varying first-order rate (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (changing conditions; ramped catalyst activity or temperature program proxy)
- Catalyst deactivation (decaying rate constant): dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t) (effective rate drops over time due to deactivation/fouling)
- Fractal/heterogeneous kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (apparent rate changes as a power of time in porous/heterogeneous media)
- Diffusion boundary-layer control proxy: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (t + c1)**c2 (rate slows with time due to growing diffusion layer)
- Periodic forcing of rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (stirring/light modulation or periodic feed effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A, then A(t) should be exponential in time (straight line in log(A) vs t), indicating first-order/pseudo-first-order kinetics.
- If dA_dt is proportional to A**2, then 1/A should be approximately linear in t, indicating bimolecular/self-reaction behavior.
- A constant negative dA_dt (independent of A) implies near-linear A(t) decrease, consistent with zero-order or externally limited regimes.
- A factor (A - c1) indicates relaxation toward a nonzero equilibrium concentration c1 (reversible reaction / steady state).
- A rational inhibition factor 1/(1 + c1*A) suggests diminishing marginal rate at high concentration (product inhibition, crowding, or transport limitation).
- Explicit time dependence in the effective rate (e.g., exp(-c*t), (t+c)^(-c)) points to non-autonomous kinetics such as catalyst deactivation or diffusion-layer growth.
- An autocatalytic term A*(c1 - A) implies an initial acceleration when A is small, followed by slowdown as A approaches c1 (self-amplification with limitation).
- Sinusoidal dependence on t indicates periodically forced kinetics; the rate oscillates even at fixed A (e.g., modulated illumination or pulsed operation).

Train NMSE          : 7.26e-15

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK13)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A + c1*_p*sin(c2*A)
Candidate formulas: 66

GT is a fixed function of **A only** (no dependence on *t*):
\[
f(A)= -0.23236613283613416\,A + 0.395876449251558\,\sin(0.5265654762365851\,A).
\]
So any matching candidate must be reducible (by choosing its free constants) to **linear-in-\(A\)** plus **a sine of a linear function of \(A\)**, with **no extra terms** (no constants, no cos, no higher powers, no logs/exp, no rational-in-\(A\)** unless they can be killed).

Below, for each candidate, I check (i) can all \(t\)-dependence be removed, and (ii) can the remaining \(A\)-dependence be made exactly \(\alpha A+\beta\sin(\gamma A)\) with \(\alpha=-0.2323...\), \(\beta=0.395876...\), \(\gamma=0.526565...\).

---

### 1. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(c2 t+c3)+c4\cos(A c5+c6)\)
- Remove \(t\): set \(c1=0\) (or \(c2=0\) but then term is \(A\cdot\text{const}\), not sine in \(A\)).
- Then left with \(A c0 + c4\cos(Ac5+c6)\): cosine cannot become sine for all \(A\) unless you allow phase shift by \(\pi/2\), but it’s still cosine-form; actually \(\cos(x-\pi/2)=\sin(x)\), so cosine *can* represent sine.
- However the GT needs **\(\sin(\gamma A)\)** with **no phase shift**. We can set \(c6=-\pi/2\) to make \(\cos(Ac5-\pi/2)=\sin(Ac5)\). Good.
- But candidate has **no way to get the correct sine amplitude while also having the correct linear term?** Yes: set \(c0=-0.232366...\), \(c4=0.395876...\), \(c5=0.526565...\), \(c6=-\pi/2\), and \(c1=0\).  
- This yields \(A c0 + c4\sin(c5 A)\), which matches GT exactly.
**→ MATCHES.**

### 2. Same as (1) plus \(c7\)
- As in (1) we can match the \(A\) and sine parts, but must also remove constant offset: set \(c7=0\).
**→ MATCHES.**

### 3. \(A c0 + A c1 + A c2\sin(c3 t+c4)+c5\cos(Ac6+c7)+c8\)
- Kill \(t\)-term: set \(c2=0\).
- Combine linear terms: \(A(c0+c1)\) can match \(-0.2323...A\).
- Convert cosine to sine via phase: choose \(c7=-\pi/2\) so \(\cos(Ac6-\pi/2)=\sin(Ac6)\).
- Kill constant: set \(c8=0\).
- Set \(c5=0.395876...\), \(c6=0.526565...\), \(c0+c1=-0.232366...\).
**→ MATCHES.**

### 4. \(A c0 + c1\cos(Ac2+c3)+c4 e^{Ac5}\sin(c6 t+c7)\)
- To remove \(t\): must set \(c4=0\) (otherwise \(\sin(c6 t+c7)\) varies with \(t\)).
- Then \(A c0 + c1\cos(Ac2+c3)\) can be turned into \(A c0 + c1\sin(Ac2)\) by setting \(c3=-\pi/2\).
- Choose \(c0=-0.232366...\), \(c1=0.395876...\), \(c2=0.526565...\), \(c3=-\pi/2\).
**→ MATCHES.**

### 5. \(A^3 c0 + A c1 + A c2\sin(Ac3+c4)+ c5\sin(c6 t+c7)\cos(Ac8+c9)\)
- Kill \(t\)-dependent product: set \(c5=0\).
- Kill cubic term: set \(c0=0\).
- Remaining: \(A c1 + A c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\) has an extra factor \(A\) multiplying the sine, but GT sine term is not multiplied by \(A\). Only way is \(c2=0\) (removes sine) which fails.
**→ NO.**

### 6. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + c2\cos(Ac3+c4)\)
- Must remove \(A^2\): set \(c0=0\).
- Convert cosine to sine via phase shift \(c4=-\pi/2\).
- Then \(A c1 + c2\sin(Ac3)\) matches with \(c1=-0.232366...\), \(c2=0.395876...\), \(c3=0.526565...\).
**→ MATCHES.**

### 7. \(A c0 + c1\cos(Ac2+c3)+c4\)
- Need no constant: set \(c4=0\).
- Convert cosine to sine: set \(c3=-\pi/2\).

**GT: -0.23237*A + 0.39588*sin(0.52657*A)**

Key observations about the GT:
- It's a function of A only (no t dependence)
- It has a linear term in A and a sin(A) term

Let me analyze each candidate. For a match, I need to be able to:
1. Eliminate any t-dependence
2. Match the functional form: linear in A + sin(linear in A)

Note: sin(c*A) can be written as cos(c*A + phase) with appropriate phase shift (cos(x - π/2) = sin(x)), so cos(c*A + c') can match sin(c*A).

**Candidates with t-dependence that can be zeroed out:**
- Terms like `A*c1*sin(c2*t + c3)`: set c1=0
- Terms like `c4*exp(c5*t)`: set c4=0
- Terms like `A*c2*t`: set c2=0
- Terms like `log(c*exp(c*t)+1)`: cannot generally be zeroed without affecting other terms

**Candidates that reduce to c*A + d*cos(e*A + f) + possible constant:**

The key identity: cos(e*A + f) can equal sin(e*A) when f = -e*A... no. cos(e*A + f) = sin(e*A + f + π/2). So c1*cos(c2*A + c3) can represent c1*sin(c2*A) by setting c3 = π/2 - (desired phase). Since GT has sin(0.527*A) with no phase shift, set c3 so that cos(c2*A + c3) = sin(c2*A), i.e., c3 = -π/2.

But GT has NO constant term. So candidates with an unavoidable constant are problematic unless the constant can be set to 0.
